    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16501547209202527362">Britt-Marie can’t stand mess. A disorganized cutlery drawer ranks high on her list of unforgivable sins. She is not one to judge others—no matter how ill-mannered, unkempt, or morally suspect they might be. It’s just that sometimes people interpret her helpful suggestions as criticisms, which is certainly not her intention. But hidden inside the socially awkward, fussy bus</span>
  <span id="freeText16501547209202527362" style="display:none">Britt-Marie can’t stand mess. A disorganized cutlery drawer ranks high on her list of unforgivable sins. She is not one to judge others—no matter how ill-mannered, unkempt, or morally suspect they might be. It’s just that sometimes people interpret her helpful suggestions as criticisms, which is certainly not her intention. But hidden inside the socially awkward, fussy busybody is a woman who has more imagination, bigger dreams, and a warmer heart that anyone around her realizes.<br /><br />When Britt-Marie walks out on her cheating husband and has to fend for herself in the miserable backwater town of Borg—of which the kindest thing one can say is that it has a road going through it—she finds work as the caretaker of a soon-to-be demolished recreation center. The fastidious Britt-Marie soon finds herself being drawn into the daily doings of her fellow citizens, an odd assortment of miscreants, drunkards, layabouts. Most alarming of all, she’s given the impossible task of leading the supremely untalented children’s soccer team to victory. In this small town of misfits, can Britt-Marie find a place where she truly belongs?</span>
  <a data-text-id="16501547209202527362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/768454-after-looking-at-a-few-reviews-i">After looking at a few reviews, I understand that Britt-Marie is a character from &quot;My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She’s Sorry&quot;. Would it be important to read that book first?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_768454'><a id="like_count_community_question_768454" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/768454?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">23 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F27406704-britt-marie-was-here">like</a></span>

</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/30963177-phillip-sawyer"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/30963177-phillip-sawyer">Phillip Sawyer</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The two books compliment each other but each can read as a stand alone. Britt Marie is such an interesting character and this book makes one realize t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The two books compliment each other but each can read as a stand alone. Britt Marie is such an interesting character and this book makes one realize that everyone's perception of the world is so different. Britt Marie's life is colored by Asperger's or OCD or her upbringing. To others, life is very different. Books like this help us realize how differently we see the same thing. Both books are excellent in their own ways. Don't miss "A Man Called Ove" also.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/15885750-innastholiel"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1435389002i/15885750._UX100_CR0,25,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/15885750-innastholiel">Innastholiel</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I actually like the ending precisely <i>because</i> Britt-Marie doesn’t end up with anyone. My reasoning for this is two-fold: <br /><br />Firstly, it surprised me. I th<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I actually like the ending precisely <i>because</i> Britt-Marie doesn’t end up with anyone. My reasoning for this is two-fold: <br /><br />Firstly, it surprised me. I thought she would end up with Sven, too. <br /><br />Secondly (and much more importantly), I find this unfolding of events remarkable. By choosing to go to Paris (was it Paris? I forget), Britt-Marie does something solely for herself, for the first time in her life. She doesn’t do it because her husband wants her to, or because she feels like she has to. No, Britt-Marie does this because <i>she</i> wants to. Because she has wanted to for much of her life. And I think by choosing this option, which is actually much scarier than staying with Kent or going out with Sven, she grows up. She learns to be her own person. And I don’t think I’ve ever read anything quite like that.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

<div id="review_1882839573" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1882839573" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1882839573?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=humour-comic-fiction">humour-comic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1882839573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer126544440125215873">I am very late to the party for this book and when I saw this in the library, I remembered how so many of my goodreads friends had read and loved this. This is a terrific tale of Britt-Marie who is 63, and who we meet as she tries to get a job because she is afraid no one will notice if she were to die, she keenly feels her isolation and loneliness. It quickly becomes clear that something is wrong from her OCD issues surrounding her manic cleaning and the manner in which she pins down her employ</span>
  <span id="freeText126544440125215873" style="display:none">I am very late to the party for this book and when I saw this in the library, I remembered how so many of my goodreads friends had read and loved this. This is a terrific tale of Britt-Marie who is 63, and who we meet as she tries to get a job because she is afraid no one will notice if she were to die, she keenly feels her isolation and loneliness. It quickly becomes clear that something is wrong from her OCD issues surrounding her manic cleaning and the manner in which she pins down her employment advisor by cooking her dinner. Her perfect world revolves around her husband, Kent, who it becomes clear has been taking her for granted and having an affair. She hasn't been working for years, being a housewife and bringing up Kent's children. She is no longer with Kent and it is going to take her some time to adjust to her new situation.<br /><br />Britt=Marie finds herself in Borg, with a temporary job as a caretaker of a recreation centre. Borg is a dying town, where everything is closing down. After a few comic setbacks, and the introduction of a great set of characters, Britt-Marie finds herself being the football coach to the children, that include Vega and Omar. There is romantic interest from Sven, the policeman. She gets closer to Sami, who is doing all that he can to look after his siblings. Before you know it, Britt=Marie is opening up, slowly beginning to live life, and is needed, particularly when things take a tragic turn. <br /><br />A lovely heartwarming, and humorous tale that snags your heartstrings for the broken Britt-Marie who lands in the broken and dying town of Borg. Each needs the other, they complement each other perfectly and both learn to survive despite the numerous obstacles in their paths. This is my first Fredrik Backman novel and I was completely charmed and bowled over by it. Highly recommended and brilliant read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="126544440125215873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/597461-elyse-walters?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/597461-elyse-walters?shelf=laugh-out-loud">laugh-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/597461-elyse-walters?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1606161600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3218650462429778331">"If Kent had been here"......<br/>Throughout this charming-tender-story, *Britt-Marie*, often reflects on her husband, Kent, who she walked out on after 40 years of marriage. She lands a job working as a caretaker at a recreation center, 12 miles away from where she and Kent lived, in a small run-down village. How she got the job is hilarious. Laugh-out-loud funny! <br/>Yet, when Britt-Marie says she misses her balcony, back home, more than anything, it was an early clue to me, that there was some deeper </span>
  <span id="freeText3218650462429778331" style="display:none">"If Kent had been here"......<br />Throughout this charming-tender-story, *Britt-Marie*, often reflects on her husband, Kent, who she walked out on after 40 years of marriage. She lands a job working as a caretaker at a recreation center, 12 miles away from where she and Kent lived, in a small run-down village. How she got the job is hilarious. Laugh-out-loud funny! <br />Yet, when Britt-Marie says she misses her balcony, back home, more than anything, it was an early clue to me, that there was some deeper loss...and I wanted to find out what that was. <br />At age 63, newly separated housewife, Britt-Marie, ( a woman who turns to cleaning as her 'vice-of-choice', as her 'coping-solution'-means), can be a stubborn, outspoken, an old 'fuddy-fart', with judgements, and rules for how everyone should be. <br />Stepping into the driver seat of her own life, without the safety belt of her husband, <br />Britt-Marie is determined she can make it on her own. Her involvement with the kids and soccer brings her purpose, joy, and friendships, that are deeply moving. <br />A rat....a snicker bar......baking soda......Faxin.... soccer.....wonderful quirky kids and town folks will have you laughing - and crying. <br />You'll also be wanting to know...what choice is Britt-Marie going to make with her life...as if the end result is what is important. But is it???? <br /><br />Fredrick Backman is a 'one-of-a-kind' writer. Clever...and wise!!!! I loved many<br />sections of his dialogue. His phrases are the heartstrings that tie this entire story together. Through Britt-Marie's journey and the people she meets, I thought about authentic friendships --the importance of giving and receiving....a little like a fair game of soccer?/! Great analogies to think like in all of Backman's novels. <br /><br />Thank You Atria Books, Netgalley, and Fredrick Backman. ( as long as he keeps writing books --I'm going to read them!!!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3218650462429778331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1799389397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11063288793763236371">This book was freaking amazing! And yeah, it made me cry . . . <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478019913ra/21021721.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478019913i/21021722._SY540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>I thought his book was wonderfully, sad. I loved Britt-Marie so much. She had these quirks that were in ways sad and in others beautiful. I would love to meet her, God would she give me a mouthful. lol *Possibly one mild spoiler*<br/><br/>She just tells it like it is: <br/><br/><b>"You have a very modern hairstyle."<br/>"What? Oh. Thanks," she replies, her fingertips moving self-consciously towards her scalp.<br/>"It's very courageous of you to wear your hair so sho</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11063288793763236371" style="display:none">This book was freaking amazing! And yeah, it made me cry . . . <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478019913ra/21021721.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478019913i/21021722._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I thought his book was wonderfully, sad. I loved Britt-Marie so much. She had these quirks that were in ways sad and in others beautiful. I would love to meet her, God would she give me a mouthful. lol *Possibly one mild spoiler*<br><br>She just tells it like it is: <br><br><b>"You have a very modern hairstyle."<br>"What? Oh. Thanks," she replies, her fingertips moving self-consciously towards her scalp.<br>"It's very courageous of you to wear your hair so short when you have such a large forehead."</b><br><br>•••••••<br><br><b>Britt-Marie wakes up on the floor. Somebody is leaning over her, saying something, but Britt-Marie's first thoughts are about the floor. She's worried that it may be dirty, and that people might think she's dead. These things happen all the time, people falling over and dying. It would be horrific, thinks Britt-Marie. To die on a dirty floor. What would people think? <br><br>"Hello, lady? Are you, you know, what's it called? Deceased?" Somebody asks, but Britt-Marie keeps focusing on the floor. <br><br>"Hello, lady? Are you, you know, dead?" Somebody repeats and makes a little whistling sound. <br><br>Britt-Marie dislikes whistling, ans she has a headache. <br>The floor smells of pizza. It would be awful to die with a headache while smelling of pizza.</b><br><br>I mean she just thinks the craziest and funniest things. Anyway, as you can read from the description, Britt-Marie decides to finally leave her husband Kent, for reasons. She goes to the unemployment office, gives them hell in her way, and proceeds to get a job in Borg. This town is in a place that's pretty much dried up and been left. She's hired to work at the recreation center until they close it up in a few weeks time. <br><br>Britt-Marie meets some wonderful characters upon arriving. She doesn't think they are so wonderful until later on. I mean she meets a rat (who later becomes her friend that she feeds nightly), thinks her car has blown up and gets hit in the head with a soccer ball. This all coming at a woman that stopped leaving the house because she just stayed and took care of things and cleaned all of the time. <br><br>Let me tell you. She should have gotten a job as a maid. Your house would never be the same again. I would hire her in a heartbeat! <br><br>The book is so moving and heartfelt. Yes, it's full of funny stuff, like Britt-Marie being turned into the children's soccer coach when she has no idea what she's doing. Her cleaning people's things until they just finally let her get on with it. But there is something else. She starts to care for these people and they care for her. She finds a place in the little community where people are just trying to survive and help each other the best they can. Although, there are some really tough lessons in the book, tough times for children, and some things so heartbreaking I can't even put it into words. <br><br>Britt-Marie also takes a little liking to the town sheriff, Sven, and him to her. Nothing ever really comes of it as. . . well it's Britt-Marie and stuff happens. I was actually hoping the ending was going to be different but I think the way it did end, was perfect for Britt-Marie's journey. It was just so happy/sad! It breaks my heart and I love all of the people in the book. I'm not going to say any more because you really need to read the book and meet these people for yourself. <br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/11/britt-marie-was-here-by-fredrik-backman.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_2741701523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2741701523" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2741701523?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781501142543" href="/book/show/30753704-britt-marie-was-here">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=illness-mental-terminal">illness-mental-terminal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=contemporary-recent">contemporary-recent</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2741701523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5898181236223720084"><i> "One morning you wake up with more life behind you than in front of you, not being able to understand how it's happened." </i><br/><br/>Aw, I loved this! This was my third Backman novel (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38205495.Beartown' title='Beartown by Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beartown</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38908034.Us_Against_You__Beartown__2_' title='Us Against You (Beartown #2) by Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Us Against You</a> being the first two)<br/>Britt-Marie is looking for a job, her first job in 60 years. After divorcing her husband, Britt-Marie is alone, with no friends, no children of her own - and she worries she will die alone and no one would be any the wiser. Hence a new job!<br/>Unfortunately due to her lack of exper</span>
  <span id="freeText5898181236223720084" style="display:none"><i> "One morning you wake up with more life behind you than in front of you, not being able to understand how it's happened." </i><br /><br />Aw, I loved this! This was my third Backman novel (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38205495.Beartown" title="Beartown by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">Beartown</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38908034.Us_Against_You__Beartown__2_" title="Us Against You (Beartown #2) by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">Us Against You</a> being the first two)<br />Britt-Marie is looking for a job, her first job in 60 years. After divorcing her husband, Britt-Marie is alone, with no friends, no children of her own - and she worries she will die alone and no one would be any the wiser. Hence a new job!<br />Unfortunately due to her lack of experience the only vacancy offered to her is the caretaker of a recreation centre in a tiny village that has been hit hard by the financial crisis. <br />Her arrival creates a bit of a stir in the town. Nearly every other business has been closed down - the post office, mechanics, supermarket etc. The one remaining business serves as everything in one - selling anything from pizza and coffee to window cleaner and car parts.<br /><br />Britt-Marie is a very strange character. She has some obsessive traits, particularly regarding her cleaning methods and her rules on manners. She does take a while to get used to, but once you do, we find she is a wonderful character with a huge heart. As she befriends the locals, and becomes the captain of the children's football team, she is embedded in Borg, and they couldn't imagine life without her.<br /><br />Overall, this was an uplifting story - just what I needed; but of course with a sharp shock which we would come to expect from Backman.<br /><br />4 stars<br /><br /><i> "People want someone to know they are here." </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5898181236223720084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1798724251" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1798724251" />
    <a title="Angela M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4685500-angela-m"><img alt="Angela M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512600770p2/4685500.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1798724251?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela M" href="/user/show/4685500-angela-m">Angela M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28436716-britt-marie-was-here">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1798724251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17351812478930537781"><br/>Over the last few years I have read and loved Fredrik Backman’s novels, but I hesitated to read this one because Britt-Marie wasn’t very likable in her brief appearance in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23604559.My_Grandmother_Asked_Me_to_Tell_You_She_s_Sorry' title='My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry by Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry</a>. But then I remembered that I didn’t like Ove very much either in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18774964.A_Man_Called_Ove' title='A Man Called Ove by Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Man Called Ove</a> until I got to know him and understood his past. I thought it was time to give Britt-Marie a chance and I’m glad I did.<br/><br/>She’s OCD and her husband Kent said that she’s “socially incompetent”. She has</span>
  <span id="freeText17351812478930537781" style="display:none"><br />Over the last few years I have read and loved Fredrik Backman’s novels, but I hesitated to read this one because Britt-Marie wasn’t very likable in her brief appearance in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23604559.My_Grandmother_Asked_Me_to_Tell_You_She_s_Sorry" title="My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry</a>. But then I remembered that I didn’t like Ove very much either in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18774964.A_Man_Called_Ove" title="A Man Called Ove by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">A Man Called Ove</a> until I got to know him and understood his past. I thought it was time to give Britt-Marie a chance and I’m glad I did.<br /><br />She’s OCD and her husband Kent said that she’s “socially incompetent”. She has her quirks about cleaning and about the order of the silverware drawer and she has no qualms with telling you just what she thinks. She suddenly finds herself alone, divorced from a cheating husband after decades. I couldn’t help but wonder how she managed to stay in this marriage for so long. How long had she deceived herself into thinking it was a good marriage ? Perhaps because of her personality, her dependence on her husband Kent. Her loneliness is heartbreaking. “She misses her balcony more than anything. You’re never quite alone when you can stand on a balcony—you have all the cars and houses and the people in the streets. You’re among them, but also not.” She was lonely even before they split up and probably longer than that. Britt-Marie worries now that she lives alone and thinks about an article in the paper about a woman found dead in her home. “She had never children and no husband and no job. No one knew she was there. If one has a job, people notice if one doesn’t show up.” <br /><br />So she takes a temporary job in a town called Borg, that is dying as a result of the failing economy and becomes the caretaker of a community center. The center has to serve as so many things because so much has closed - the pizzeria, a bar, a minimart, and more . There’s not much left except the soccer team and a few stalwarts who don’t want to give up. Before we know it, Britt-Marie becomes the soccer coach and so much more to a cast of quirky characters. She becomes their friend and they become hers and they give more to each other than any of them would have expected. It’s all at once funny and sad and uplifting. The initially unlikable Britt-Marie becomes one of Backman’s lovable characters. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17351812478930537781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1694040174" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1694040174" />
    <a title="Esil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3643764-esil"><img alt="Esil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443746908p2/3643764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1694040174?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Esil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Esil" href="/user/show/3643764-esil">Esil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1694040174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16351215181345476595">3+ stars. I loved Fredrik Backman's first two books, so I went to some lengths to get a copy of his third book, Britt-Marie Was Here. I begged shamelessly on a couple of sites for advance copies. When that didn't work, I found a copy while on a trip to New York because the book was not yet available in Canada. The problem with high anticipation is that it can sometimes breed disappointment. I liked Britt-Marie Was Here, but I didn't love it the same way I loved its predecessors. Unfortunately, i</span>
  <span id="freeText16351215181345476595" style="display:none">3+ stars. I loved Fredrik Backman's first two books, so I went to some lengths to get a copy of his third book, Britt-Marie Was Here. I begged shamelessly on a couple of sites for advance copies. When that didn't work, I found a copy while on a trip to New York because the book was not yet available in Canada. The problem with high anticipation is that it can sometimes breed disappointment. I liked Britt-Marie Was Here, but I didn't love it the same way I loved its predecessors. Unfortunately, it feels like Backman developed a bit of formula in A Man Called Ove, and Britt-Marie Was Here followed that formula without any original deviations. Britt-Marie is not a bad person, but she is very rigid in her devotion to cleanliness and order. When her marriage falls apart, she moves to a tiny dying town where she is employed as a caretaker in a community centre. There are many scenes involving misunderstandings between Britt-Marie and the town's people. Over time, they get to know and appreciate each other, and are ultimately transformed by each other. Overall, the tone is light, but there are a few events -- especially at the end -- that are more dramatic. Backman is good at the details, and this is what saved the book for me. Britt-Marie's relationship with a group of children, soccer, a rat and alcohol are the details that give life to the story. But still I didn't find myself as wowed or engaged as with Backman's last two books. I suspect that I would have liked this one more if it had been my first Backman book. I hope Backman brings a bit more originality to the narrative structure of his next book -- regardless, I suspect that I will chase it yet again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16351215181345476595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1626514920" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626514920" />
    <a title="Candi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3639005-candi"><img alt="Candi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585187464p2/3639005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1626514920?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candi" href="/user/show/3639005-candi">Candi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28436716-britt-marie-was-here">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=contemporary-literary">contemporary-literary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1626514920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14472692496021011516"><i>"There’s a lot you can’t know about a person until you become one with her. What her capabilities are. The courage she has."</i><br/><br/>I first met Britt-Marie in Backman’s novel <b>My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She’s Sorry</b>. She wasn’t exactly loveable in that book, so I was prepared to meet yet another grumpy and somewhat eccentric character in this one. Well, she was just as I imagined she would be! While I thought perhaps I wasn’t going to be inclined to read an entire book about her royal crankypants</span>
  <span id="freeText14472692496021011516" style="display:none"><i>"There’s a lot you can’t know about a person until you become one with her. What her capabilities are. The courage she has."</i><br /><br />I first met Britt-Marie in Backman’s novel <b>My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She’s Sorry</b>. She wasn’t exactly loveable in that book, so I was prepared to meet yet another grumpy and somewhat eccentric character in this one. Well, she was just as I imagined she would be! While I thought perhaps I wasn’t going to be inclined to read an entire book about her royal crankypants, my sentiments quickly reversed. What first caught my attention was the humor, despite my qualms about Britt-Marie. Then I slowly began to realize what makes this woman tick - I started to look at the world from her point of view. I came to an understanding; I even nodded my head in agreement at some of her observations. <i>"Britt-Marie can’t for the life of her understand why anyone would choose to practice an outdoor sport while wearing white jerseys. It’s barbaric."</i> I know, right?!! I don’t know how many bottles of Advanced Shout I’ve gone through since my kids began to play soccer! Eventually, I was sucked into the story and wanted to make friends with Britt-Marie. <br /><br />At the age of sixty-three, Britt-Marie is on her own. She has left behind a cheating husband and is in search of employment for the first time in decades. Arriving in the run-down town of Borg, she may not really be making a step in the right direction. After all, how can one gain a sense of independence when there are very few opportunities and the economy has shut down the majority of the businesses in town? <i>"… the only two noticeable things in Borg are soccer and the pizzeria, because these tend to be the last things to abandon humanity."</i> Here she meets a zany cast of characters (even a rat!) and learns more than she ever fancied about the game of soccer. As the children rally around her, Britt-Marie finds herself in charge of the motley crew that call themselves a team. Then, what began as a light-hearted story turns into a truly heartwarming tale about what it means to stand together despite all odds, learning to forge friendships in the most unlikely places. Fredrik Backman manages to create such endearing characters; ones that won’t soon be forgotten. I have two more of his novels to go, and hope he has many more yet to follow. <br /> <br /><i>"She wonders how much space a person has left in her soul to change herself, once she gets older. What people does she still have to meet, what will they see in her, and what will they make her see in herself?"</i> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14472692496021011516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2042044496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2042044496" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4125660-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316269997p2/4125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2042044496?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/4125660-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2042044496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9962071079553112006">Those of you who have read My Grandmother Told Me to Tell You She's Sorry, will remember Britt-Marie. For those of you who have not yet read it, I advise reading it first. That book gives you the background of Britt-Marie while she was still married. <br/><br/>This book starts off with her looking for a job. She hasn't worked in years. She's been a devoted wife, giving over her entire life to Kent. But Kent hasn't appreciated her brand of obsessive loyalty and has had an affair and she has left him. Britt</span>
  <span id="freeText9962071079553112006" style="display:none">Those of you who have read My Grandmother Told Me to Tell You She's Sorry, will remember Britt-Marie. For those of you who have not yet read it, I advise reading it first. That book gives you the background of Britt-Marie while she was still married. <br /><br />This book starts off with her looking for a job. She hasn't worked in years. She's been a devoted wife, giving over her entire life to Kent. But Kent hasn't appreciated her brand of obsessive loyalty and has had an affair and she has left him. Britt-Marie is a weird bird. She's socially awkward, more than a little obsessIve on how things should be done and totally tactless. But you grow to love her. Likewise the other characters. Somebody is especially hilarious. She's the town’s jack of all trades, the fixer, the one who gets things done as long as you aren't too particular about how. <br /><br />Backman has the ability to capture the feel of a place with very few words. Borg is a town where almost everything has closed down. “The only two noticeable things in Borg are soccer and the pizzeria, because these tend to be the last things to abandon humanity.”<br /><br />This book will have you laughing and crying, sometimes at the same time. <br /><br />Another wonderful book by Backman. Highly recommend. <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6914795476627978076"><b>4 Faxin Stars</b><br/><br/>This was my first ever Fredrik Backman book. <br/>And I absolutely loved Backman's writing style. <br/>I loved the story. <br/>I loved all the supporting characters...<br/>and I REALLY loved Britt-Marie. <br/><br/><i>"At a certain age almost all the questions a person asks him or herself are really just about one thing: how should you live your life?</i><br/><br/>But really, how should we? <br/>Something to think about. <br/>Something this book definitely made me think about.</span>

<div id="review_2444604112" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2444604112" />
    <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read"><img alt="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580849831p2/24156068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2444604112?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read">Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2444604112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17741897198019207"><b>4, no I'm not ugly crying and laughing at the same time, I swear I'm not crazy stars.</b><br/><br/>This is my first Backman novel (I know, I'm behind the times) and to be honest, I was unsure how I was going to feel about this for the first couple of chapters. I actually genuinely liked Britt-Marie right off the bat but I wasn't in a particular mood for something depressing and it felt like that might be the direction this was going to take. I'm very happy to say, I was very wrong in this case. <br/><br/>This is about </span>
  <span id="freeText17741897198019207" style="display:none"><b>4, no I'm not ugly crying and laughing at the same time, I swear I'm not crazy stars.</b><br /><br />This is my first Backman novel (I know, I'm behind the times) and to be honest, I was unsure how I was going to feel about this for the first couple of chapters. I actually genuinely liked Britt-Marie right off the bat but I wasn't in a particular mood for something depressing and it felt like that might be the direction this was going to take. I'm very happy to say, I was very wrong in this case. <br /><br />This is about Britt-Marie, a 63-year-old divorcee, seemingly starting her life over. She finds a new job in a disintegrating town called Borg. She is exceptionally neurotic, she has <i>many</i> rules she believes one should live by and calling her "quirky" is putting it quite mildly. However, Britt-Marie is also incredibly strong-willed and determined. She has lived her life patently unappreciated by her husband Kent - he took no notice of her cleaning, her superior use of baking soda or the importance of a properly made bed *same tho*, to the point of being wholly <i>unnoticed</i>.<br /><br /><b>“She wonders how much space a person has left in her soul to change herself, once she gets older. What people does she still have to meet, what will they see in her, and what will they make her see in herself?"</b><br /><br />As it turns out, there is <i>a lot</i> of space left in Britt-Marie's soul to change, to grow and to become someone she's always wanted to be. This is about finding yourself again, about personal growth, about being passionate about <b>your</b> life. Backman has an exceptional command of language, an ability to wield words in the most useful way to tell whatever part of the story he needs to. Everything is concise and to the point but it is done in a way that doesn't sacrifice emotion or detail. <br /><br />In the end, this was actually an incredibly ordinary story but Backman found a way to show the beauty in that. Life, for the most part, is fairly ordinary with a few extraordinary moments sprinkled in and we have to find the beauty in that ourselves. This was a happy, refreshing and unexpected read about friendship, hope and standing together. I think it's worth picking up for Backman's writing alone but I enjoyed Britt-Marie and I think most of us could find a little bit of ourselves in her as well. Keep on doin' you girl, you're good just the way you are.<br /><br /><b>“All passion is childish. It's banal and naive. It's nothing we learn; it's instinctive, and so it overwhelms us. Overturns us. It bears us away in a flood. All other emotions belong to earth, but passion inhabits the universe.<br />That is the reason why passion is worth something, not for what it gives us but for what it demands we risk. Our dignity. The puzzlement of others and their condescending, shaking heads” </b><br /><br />If you're asking yourself "do I really want to read a book about a neurotic 63-year-old woman finding herself?" the answer is a resounding <i>hell yes you do</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17741897198019207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

His better-known book, "A Man Called Ove," has more straightforwardly good and bad characters that are easier to like and dislike, then ending a crowd pleaser. Here he takes on the monumental challenge of nuance -- characters which are both good and bad, endings that are not pat -- & he does admirably.</span>

<div id="review_2906292089" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2906292089" />
    <a title="Swaroop Kanti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/100264072-swaroop-kanti"><img alt="Swaroop Kanti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594460958p2/100264072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2906292089?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Swaroop Kanti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Swaroop Kanti" href="/user/show/100264072-swaroop-kanti">Swaroop Kanti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781501142550" href="/book/show/27778672-britt-marie-was-here">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906292089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17206199227295961054">An amazingly <b>well-written, deep, meaningful and adorable book!</b><br/><br/>In the beginning, the storyline feels difficult and awkward, which is very similar to the main character, Britt-Marie. And, then somewhere in between, this book changes into a wonderful reading experience. It does feel like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6485178.Fredrik_Backman' title='Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fredrik Backman</a> intentionally kept the storyline to be frustrating at the beginning, as those who continue to read past the initial chapters, are actually going to understand who is Britt-Marie and what exactly she</span>
  <span id="freeText17206199227295961054" style="display:none">An amazingly <b>well-written, deep, meaningful and adorable book!</b><br /><br />In the beginning, the storyline feels difficult and awkward, which is very similar to the main character, Britt-Marie. And, then somewhere in between, this book changes into a wonderful reading experience. It does feel like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6485178.Fredrik_Backman" title="Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">Fredrik Backman</a> intentionally kept the storyline to be frustrating at the beginning, as those who continue to read past the initial chapters, are actually going to understand who is Britt-Marie and what exactly she is going through. <br /><br />An honest, touching and straight-forward book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27406704.Britt_Marie_Was_Here" title="Britt-Marie Was Here by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">Britt-Marie Was Here</a> is fun to read and, as with any of the other books by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6485178.Fredrik_Backman" title="Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">Fredrik Backman</a>, this also has a lot of takeaways:<br /><blockquote> <i> "An unreasonable amount of paperwork is required these days just to be a human being."<br /><br />"It is difficult to know when love blooms; suddenly one day you wake up and it`s in full flower."<br /><br />"It`s easier to stay optimistic if you never have to clear up the mess afterwards."<br /><br />"Soccer is a curious game, because it doesn`t ask to be loved. It demands it."<br /><br />"At a certain age almost all the questions a person ask him or herself are really just about one thing: how should you live your life?"<br /><br />"That is the reason why passion is worth something, not for what it gives us but for what it demands that we risk." </i></blockquote>  <br /><i>
  <b>"Because if we don`t forgive those we love, then what is left? What is love if it`s not loving our lovers even when they don`t deserve it?"</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17206199227295961054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1627426190" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1627426190" />
    <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong"><img alt="Susanne  Strong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583087410p2/4514828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1627426190?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne  Strong" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong">Susanne  Strong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=2016-five-star-books">2016-five-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1627426190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12908766145395956701">Britt-Marie was Here is the best book I've read this year. Simply put, it is fantastic. <br/><br/>Britt-Marie is difficult, frustrating and socially awkward. She is also insensitive and kind of rude. A minor character in My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry, Britt-Marie was instantly disliked in that book and is not well liked in the beginning of this one either. However, Fredrik Backman has this endearing way of making old curmudgeons likeable and being extremely successful at it (i.e. Ove and</span>
  <span id="freeText12908766145395956701" style="display:none">Britt-Marie was Here is the best book I've read this year. Simply put, it is fantastic. <br /><br />Britt-Marie is difficult, frustrating and socially awkward. She is also insensitive and kind of rude. A minor character in My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry, Britt-Marie was instantly disliked in that book and is not well liked in the beginning of this one either. However, Fredrik Backman has this endearing way of making old curmudgeons likeable and being extremely successful at it (i.e. Ove and Britt-Marie). Her character, her ocd, her social ineptitude.. they grow on you. Here, we find out why she is the way she is and we discover that, due to her childhood and her marriage, she has felt invisible her whole life. She has trouble figuring out who she really is and is fanatical simply because it is the only thing she can control. Upon losing everything, she decides to find a job and is forced to move to a small town. In the process she finds a sense of humor, discovers that she is capable of making friends and also finds her sense of self. <br /><br />Fredrik Backman's A Man Called Ove was one of my favorite books ever. His writing style is smart, funny, quirky and just downright amazing. His characters are rich, well developed and beloved. In addition to Britt-Marie, Vega, Somebody, Bank, Sami and "the girl from the unemployment office" lent heart and soul to the story and gave Britt-Marie exactly what she needed: friends and reasons to go have at it. <br /><br />I didn't think it was possible for Mr. Backman to write another book that I'd love as much as "Ove" but if truth be told, I love this one more. It was truly phenomenal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12908766145395956701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=owned">owned</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1612408520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9677829715602373620"><i>The publisher sent me a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. All thoughts & opinions are my own.</i><br/><br/>You guys. You GUYS! This was one of the sweetest books I have ever read. After reading Fredrik Backman's first novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18774964.A_Man_Called_Ove' title='A Man Called Ove by Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'> A Man Called Ove</a> earlier this year, I was contacted by the publisher to read & review his latest release, <i>Britt-Marie Was Here.</i> Even though I wasn't obsessed with <i>A Man Called Ove</i>, I thought it was incredibly quirky, funny and touching, so I figured I would give this one</span>
  <span id="freeText9677829715602373620" style="display:none"><i>The publisher sent me a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. All thoughts &amp; opinions are my own.</i><br /><br />You guys. You GUYS! This was one of the sweetest books I have ever read. After reading Fredrik Backman's first novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18774964.A_Man_Called_Ove" title="A Man Called Ove by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener"> A Man Called Ove</a> earlier this year, I was contacted by the publisher to read &amp; review his latest release, <i>Britt-Marie Was Here.</i> Even though I wasn't obsessed with <i>A Man Called Ove</i>, I thought it was incredibly quirky, funny and touching, so I figured I would give this one a shot.<br /><br />And I'm so glad I did. I liked it even more than I expected to. It's a heartwarming story about Britt-Marie, a rather particular elderly woman who finds herself thrust into a new situation in life. She moves to a new town, gets a job and makes new friends in unlikely ways. Even though the theme of our impact on each other's lives is explore often in literature, it's one of my favorites and always such a great reminder. And this story totally did it justice. <br /><br />If you're looking for something that will make you laugh, cry and come out on the other side with a bit more optimism, I would definitely recommend this book. I can't wait to check out Backman's other novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23604559.My_Grandmother_Asked_Me_to_Tell_You_She_s_Sorry" title="My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener"> My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry</a>, hopefully sooner rather than later.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3022834341" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26175098-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453924875p2/26175098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3022834341?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/26175098-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28436716-britt-marie-was-here">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=libby-has">libby-has</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=scandanavian">scandanavian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=award-winner-nominee">award-winner-nominee</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3022834341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer638184414717634289">Having really enjoyed My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She’s Sorry I couldn’t wait to get my hands on a copy of Britt-Marie Was Here. Britt-Marie did not come across as very likeable in the former novel, but by the end of the book I had a better understanding of her. I loved her in in Britt-Marie Was Here.<br/><br/>Britt-Marie is a strange duck. She is repressed and socially inept (understatement). She has OCD traits and miserable self-esteem. At age 63, she suddenly finds herself on her own in a teeny</span>
  <span id="freeText638184414717634289" style="display:none">Having really enjoyed My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She’s Sorry I couldn’t wait to get my hands on a copy of Britt-Marie Was Here. Britt-Marie did not come across as very likeable in the former novel, but by the end of the book I had a better understanding of her. I loved her in in Britt-Marie Was Here.<br /><br />Britt-Marie is a strange duck. She is repressed and socially inept (understatement). She has OCD traits and miserable self-esteem. At age 63, she suddenly finds herself on her own in a teeny little town in Sweden. How can she possibly survive? <br /><br />It amazes me how such a simply written novel could be so moving and inspirational. It even drew out the tears. This book is not action-filled. Like the other Backman book I read, it is a character study, a slice of life, and a story full of introspection on the part of the protagonist. There is quirkiness, whimsy, and humor, as well as wisdom, insight, and life lessons to be learned. <br /><br />The cast of characters is priceless. I was especially fond of Vera, Sami, Somebody, Sven, Bank, and the rat. Each one plays an important role in Britt-Marie’s journey to come back to herself.<br /><br />I was not totally cool with the ambiguous ending, but no stars are lost as the ambiguous ending is beautifully ambiguous and touched my heart. But dang-- where is my epilogue???<br /><br />This is a sweet, heartfelt story. I recommend it for everyone not looking for heavy action or a super complex plot. The book may be even more enjoyable if one reads My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She’s Sorry first. Britt-Marie and her husband Kent are featured in that book as well. <br /><br />Now on to Ove once my number comes up at the library!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="638184414717634289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9091273404069367552" style="display:none">My inauguration into the world of Backman.<br />I wasn't sure about it for the first 50 pages thinking this character is whacked and do I really want to read about a 64 year old woman who is only just finding herself after years of repression? It turned out, yes I do. <br /><br />Britt-Marie is a hot mess. She's left her husband - which was well overdue- but is lost in a world nonexistent to others. She's never worked outside of the home and she has cleaning OCD. She's really odd - her thoughts; her behaviours. <br />She takes a job in Borg - a village dying with businesses closing up but here ironically, is where her life begins.<br />What a quirky character. Backman's style took a little getting used to - I can see why some readers may have not been riveted. I'm not sure I would have picked this one up if I'd read his others - which I plan on doing. While it did keep my interest, I felt it was just skimming the surface. As for the ending, I don't like coming to my own conclusions.<br />3* as Britt is a memorable character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9091273404069367552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2106919289" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2106919289" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2106919289?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=1-fiction">1-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=9-read-2018-09-september">9-read-2018-09-september</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2106919289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10232147271379326775">Author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6485178.Fredrik_Backman' title='Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fredrik Backman</a> is in my TOP 5 writers of all time. I've read 4 of his books now, and they always have a profound impact on me. I'm hoping to finish reading them all this year which is why <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27406704.Britt_Marie_Was_Here' title='Britt-Marie Was Here by Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Britt-Marie Was Here</a> made it to my September TBR. If you're familiar with his work, it's a combination of 'A Man Called Ove' and 'Beartown' in terms of the love of sport, the human condition's intensity, and the desire for a different life. All in all, I gave it 4.25 stars as it was better than a 4 but </span>
  <span id="freeText10232147271379326775" style="display:none">Author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6485178.Fredrik_Backman" title="Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">Fredrik Backman</a> is in my TOP 5 writers of all time. I've read 4 of his books now, and they always have a profound impact on me. I'm hoping to finish reading them all this year which is why <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27406704.Britt_Marie_Was_Here" title="Britt-Marie Was Here by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">Britt-Marie Was Here</a> made it to my September TBR. If you're familiar with his work, it's a combination of 'A Man Called Ove' and 'Beartown' in terms of the love of sport, the human condition's intensity, and the desire for a different life. All in all, I gave it 4.25 stars as it was better than a 4 but I couldn't round up to a 5 on this one...<br /><br />Britt-Marie is in her early 60s and has left her husband, Kent, after she caught him cheating on her via the other woman taking him to the hospital as he had a heart attack. Although she's independent, Britt-Marie has been cared for too long by others to know exactly how to survive on her own. She succeeds on many levels when she moves to a town, Borg, not too far away from home to get her first outside-of-the-home job since she was a waitress right after high school and right before marrying Kent. In Borg, life is basically listless, scarce, and penniless. It's been hit by a financial crisis and no one has money for anything. Britt-Marie does her best to find a way to make the move to a new job and a new residence something positive, but it doesn't go very smoothly at first. In time, she evolves into a more open-minded individual, yet her core beliefs remain stalwart. She's ornery but lovable, kind but too direct, thoughtful but not very worldly. It makes her human like the rest of us.<br /><br />Backman's style is usually on-point when it comes to connecting with his readers. This book is no exception; however, there were several sections with either translation issues (it wasn't originally written in English) or a purposed attempt to write in a different manner from what he's shown us before. Examples include frequent repetition of words or phrases that it became too obvious. Was it intended or just the translation -- I'm not certain, but it caused me to stumble a fair number of times. Another concern was a general casualization (yep, I'm making up words) of some characters where I wasn't quite sure if I wanted to root for them or ignore them. The end result was some felt too similar while others felt strong but underused given their purpose in the story.<br /><br />That said, the rest is amazing. I felt the connection between Britt-Marie and everyone she meets who changes her life. I saw the lackluster relationship with Kent but understood why she couldn't leave him. I felt the pain of what her childhood resulted in when it came to how she viewed herself and let others view her. I adored the way she persistently nagged the unemployment office employee only to become the woman's bright hope for the future. It's only when an author is an innate talent can these types of well-embedded structures, depths, and life perceptions be truly integrated into a story. That's where, how, and why Backman leads the race when it comes to producing truly remarkable stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10232147271379326775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1865882242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1865882242" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1865882242?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28436716-britt-marie-was-here">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1865882242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8638527750961885265">Brit-Marie Was Here by Fredrik Backman is a 2016 Atria Books publication. <br/><br/>Believe it or not, this is my first novel by this author! I’ve heard so many wonderful things about his novels and can’t think of a better way to start off 2017 than by finally joining the Fredrik Backman club! <br/><br/>Brit-Marie was Here is just an all around wonderful story! I laughed, got angry, worried, and cried, but closed the book feeling like I’d been on a special journey with Britt-Marie in her quest for purpose, belongin</span>
  <span id="freeText8638527750961885265" style="display:none">Brit-Marie Was Here by Fredrik Backman is a 2016 Atria Books publication. <br /><br />Believe it or not, this is my first novel by this author! I’ve heard so many wonderful things about his novels and can’t think of a better way to start off 2017 than by finally joining the Fredrik Backman club! <br /><br />Brit-Marie was Here is just an all around wonderful story! I laughed, got angry, worried, and cried, but closed the book feeling like I’d been on a special journey with Britt-Marie in her quest for purpose, belonging and overdue self-discovery. <br /><br />This novel is delightful and very quirky, with oddball characters, and situations, but underneath the humor there is an underlying seriousness, which explores relationships, loneliness, the desire to be needed and loved, appreciated, to make a real difference, and to matter to someone. <br /><br /> Britt-Marie is not exactly the warmest person in the world when we first meet her, but I still liked her. I knew immediately that she had OCD, which explains a great deal, but she’s also socially awkward. <br /><br />She’s devoted her entire life to her husband, Kent, finding pleasure… or was it release? In keeping her house tidy, enjoying her balcony, and raising Kent’s children. She has no friendships, and everything in her life is orderly, clean, and on a perfectly timed schedule, until…<br /><br />Britt-Marie discovers her beloved Kent is having an affair. She simply walks away without a word. She begins looking for a job at the age of sixty-three, with no formal education and no work experience, in an economic down period. <br /><br />However, she does manage to find temporary work at a recreation center, that is about to be shut down, in the small hamlet of ‘Borg’. This job, the town, and its residents will slowly draw Britt-Marie out of her shell, and will enrich her life via a string of wild adventures and through the game of soccer, a sport she initially resented and despised. <br /><br />This book is so adorable and sweet!! <br /><br /> There are so many poignant elements, themes, and life lessons to explore and think about. The characters are so well drawn, the language and prose is near perfect, as is the pacing and the hysterically funny, yet touching, razor sharp dialogue. <br /><br />Britt-Marie is a character I will remember for a long time to come and am so happy I was able to meet her and experience her awakening and personal growth. I hope we can touch base with her again someday!! <br /><br />4 stars<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8638527750961885265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1631477506" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1631477506" />
    <a title="Lori " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26424937-lori"><img alt="Lori " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559993723p2/26424937.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1631477506?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori " href="/user/show/26424937-lori">Lori </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26424937-lori?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1631477506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10033484439244971357">Ha, I loved it. It has the generous spirit and humor of "A Man Called Ove" and the heart-tugging emotion that sneaks up on you -- so powerfully employed in "My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry" -- that's Backman's signature. His repetitive, deceptively simplistic style holds within it a world of love and sorrow. His ability to move the reader is extraordinary. <br/><br/>The first few chapters of "Britt-Marie" are slow going. It's wonderful seeing her in a wholly new situation, adapting to circ</span>
  <span id="freeText10033484439244971357" style="display:none">Ha, I loved it. It has the generous spirit and humor of "A Man Called Ove" and the heart-tugging emotion that sneaks up on you -- so powerfully employed in "My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She's Sorry" -- that's Backman's signature. His repetitive, deceptively simplistic style holds within it a world of love and sorrow. His ability to move the reader is extraordinary. <br /><br />The first few chapters of "Britt-Marie" are slow going. It's wonderful seeing her in a wholly new situation, adapting to circumstances beyond her limited imagination. It takes a little while to get a handle on the town of Borg and its quirky inhabitants. That's because Borg is an unusual place and because Britt-Marie is wary of each new person and every new situation. Once the book gets going it hits notes high and low with the precision of a soccer ball hitting a soda can. I laughed, I cried, I rooted for Britt-Marie and the quirky inhabitants of Borg all the way through the unexpected, and perfect, ending.<br /><br />I'm in awe of Fredrik Backman, whose novels are fresh and original, funny and full of heart. He gets us to love his characters via their tics and faults, not despite them. Ha. I can't wait for his fourth novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10033484439244971357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
