<div id="review_1680140034" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1680140034" />
    <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice"><img alt="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509647506p2/30817744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1680140034?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice">Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=2016">2016</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1680140034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4498570200728533801">An intriguing read. I would not call it hilarious, but it was certainly humorous and heart-warming.<br/><br/><i>'If you merely drive through Borg its easy to notice only the places that have been closed down. You have to slow down to see what's still there. There are people in Borg. There are rats and Zimmer-frames and greenhouses. Wooden fences and white jerseys and lit candles. Newly laid turf and sunny stories.'<i><br/><br/>This is no doubt true of many small towns around the world, but Borg is the unlikely place wher</i></i></span>
  <span id="freeText4498570200728533801" style="display:none">An intriguing read. I would not call it hilarious, but it was certainly humorous and heart-warming.<br /><br /><i>'If you merely drive through Borg its easy to notice only the places that have been closed down. You have to slow down to see what's still there. There are people in Borg. There are rats and Zimmer-frames and greenhouses. Wooden fences and white jerseys and lit candles. Newly laid turf and sunny stories.'<i><br /><br />This is no doubt true of many small towns around the world, but Borg is the unlikely place where Britt-Marie (only her deceased sister was ever allowed to call her Britt) finds herself after her marriage disintegrates. More than a little OCD, Britt-Marie judges people by their cutlery drawers and is obsessed with Bicarb of Soda and Faxin window-cleaner. She has precise and regimented ways of doing things "after all, we're not animals, are we?"<br /><br />For the fastidious Britt-Marie, this new world of noisy children, muddy floors, and a roommate who is a rat (literally), is a hard adjustment. And she finds herself doing things she never would have believed she would do, and befriending and being befriended by people she would never have associated with in the past. And then she has to make a choice....<br /><br />I could see a little of myself in Britt-Marie at times, there is probably a little of her in most of us. <br /><br />She left me smiling, and curious to see where her next adventure will take her.<br /><br />Thank you Glenda Henry for this precious birthday present.</i></i></span>

<div id="review_1711216241" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711216241" />
    <a title="Margitte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte"><img alt="Margitte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361772481p2/7481492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711216241?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margitte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margitte" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte">Margitte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=community">community</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=family-sagas">family-sagas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711216241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6034698928161564493">Britt-Marie was sort of a married woman. Sort of. If it wasn't for her husband's heart attack while being with his mistress, Britt-Marie might still have been happily locked away in her forty-year-old marriage, where she loved her balcony and her total dedication to her husband. She had no friends, did not go outside her apartment, and never questioned her needy behavior. As long as her husband was completely depended on her mothering skills, she was happy. Life was under control. Sort of. <br/><br/>It wa</span>
  <span id="freeText6034698928161564493" style="display:none">Britt-Marie was sort of a married woman. Sort of. If it wasn't for her husband's heart attack while being with his mistress, Britt-Marie might still have been happily locked away in her forty-year-old marriage, where she loved her balcony and her total dedication to her husband. She had no friends, did not go outside her apartment, and never questioned her needy behavior. As long as her husband was completely depended on her mothering skills, she was happy. Life was under control. Sort of. <br /><br />It was very important that her cutlery drawer was perfectly organized, forks, knives, spoons, and everything cleaned everyday with vinegar and baking soda and only Faxin for the windows. Coffee in plastic mugs and plastic teaspoons had the same value as roadkill in her book. Tables without coasters were so animalistic. Everyday had its penciled-in list. Nothing happened without it. Everything on it happened. Non-negotiable. She ate her cold dinner at exactly six o'clock in the evening. Civilized people do that. Her balcony was astonishingly, astonishingly presentable. Her own special space. She laughed inward. Always. Not a sound was heard on the outside. <br /><br />After forty years of being a housewife and completing hundreds of crosswords, she regarded herself as a highly educated person and did not think it would be difficult to find a job as a sixty-three-year-old woman. Her husband, Kent, said the economic recession was over. How difficult could it be?<br /><br />As a young girl she was in an accident in which her sister died. Her parents hardly knew that Britt-Marie stayed alive. They slowly died themselves, leaving her, the unimportant child, behind. But the accident also changed Britt-Marie's behavior, leaving her with almost a lite form of Asperger's or Autism syndrome. Her life needed to be strictly structured and her obsessive compulsive tendencies prevented her from being socially adaptable. Soccer was an enemy. It was Kent's only passion in life, apart from being married to his entrepreneurial business and his mistress. <br /><br />In her solo world she just took off, leaving Kent to find his clothes and shaving utensils after she rearranged it. No she did not hide it. She applied for jobs at a job seeking agency and coincidentally found one as a caretaker of a community center in the dying town, Borg. <br /><br /><i>It was a community built along the road, and that was the kindest thing one can say about it. There was a closed-down chemist, a closed-down soccer field, a closed-down school, a closed-down health center, a closed-down supermarket, and a road that bears away in two different directions ...</i><br /><br />Kent was not there anymore. And Kent was wrong about the economic recession. Her safety net was gone. A coffee machine became a thread which she had to attack. Only Kent made the coffee at home. But, as she stopped in front of her new building, her car exploded, ka-boom, ... and a soccer ball hit her on the head ... It was the beginning of the rest of her life. Borg and Britt-Marie would never be the same again.<br /><br />As the two previous books, this was a really good read. I enjoyed the first book <i>'A Man Called Ove'</i> the most by far. The second book, <i>'My Grandmother Told Me To Tell You She's Sorry'</i> also charmed me further into the writings of this author. I laughed and cried for Britt-Marie and her new town. I was captured in the ambiance of the pizziera cum post office cum hairdresser saloon cum car repair shop with the characters filing its spaces on a daily basis. Even that rat without-a-name, became lovable. Pathos reigned. It was impossible to not feel the strong deeper undercurrents of bonding keeping the town going in difficult times. In the end I did not know if I wanted to laugh or cry. It was not that simple after all.<br /><br />Frederik Backman has a Pandora's box filled with intricate souls he blows life into when he presents them as protagonists in his books to his now addicted readers. He knows we cannot live without them! Let the next book be here soon, please.<br /><br />I absolutely loved this book. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6034698928161564493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1553260464" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1553260464" />
    <a title="Cheri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106692-cheri"><img alt="Cheri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601402708p2/106692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1553260464?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheri" href="/user/show/106692-cheri">Cheri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28880600-britt-marie-was-here">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jeff Giles</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1553260464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9217547907387279288">Britt-Marie is the sort of person who likes things just so. She can’t abide a disorganized cutlery drawer, being offered “milk” in tiny disposable cartons, plastic mugs, plastic teaspoons. She is, if nothing else, fastidious. <br/><br/>“’Milk and Sugar?’ the girl asks, pouring some coffee into a plastic mug. Britt-Marie doesn’t judge anyone. Far from it. But who would behave like that? A plastic mug! Are we at war?”<br/><br/>Britt-Marie begins this journey as a 63-year old woman who has just moved out of her flat w</span>
  <span id="freeText9217547907387279288" style="display:none">Britt-Marie is the sort of person who likes things just so. She can’t abide a disorganized cutlery drawer, being offered “milk” in tiny disposable cartons, plastic mugs, plastic teaspoons. She is, if nothing else, fastidious. <br /><br />“’Milk and Sugar?’ the girl asks, pouring some coffee into a plastic mug. Britt-Marie doesn’t judge anyone. Far from it. But who would behave like that? A plastic mug! Are we at war?”<br /><br />Britt-Marie begins this journey as a 63-year old woman who has just moved out of her flat with her husband, Kent, and begins a new life working in a village that has very little, in terms of modern conveniences, to offer. It’s a community on the verge of non-existence in a place her mother would have described as “the back of beyond.” The few people and shops left are taking on additional responsibilities, the pizzeria serving multiple roles as other places close. <br /><br />In her new role as caretaker of the recreation center, Britt-Marie finds herself slowing finding herself warming up to the residents of Borg, The young people have little to do except play soccer, and as she warms up to a few select residents (including a rat), the residents begin to involve her in their lives, their worries, as they begin to open themselves to her, she begins to feel more “at home.” Still, there is Kent in the back of her mind, her philandering husband who she has spent most of her life taking care of. Now, she must take care of herself, she must be in charge of herself and her life. Her new life. <br /><br />“The reason for her love of maps. It’s half worn away, the dot, and the red color is bleached. Yet it’s there, flung down there on the map halfway between the lower left corner and its center, and next to it is written, 'You are here.' Sometimes it’s easier to go on living, not even knowing who you are, when at least you know precisely where you are while you go on not knowing.”<br /><br />With so many years of life with Kent behind her, she is still often torn between her old life, its comforts and routines, and this new life where virtually everything is new for Britt-Marie, new friends, new routines, new feelings. She has a new purpose, a newfound joy in herself, and her new friends, in this new community where she has made her home. She feels needed, she no longer feels invisible. <br /><br />“At a certain age almost all the questions a person asks him or herself are really just about one thing: How should you live your life?”<br /><br />Fredrik Backman has written yet another captivating story with terrific characters that are easy to give your heart to. If you read “A Man Called Ove” and / or “My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She’s Sorry” and enjoyed them, this is a must read. If you haven’t read his former novels, “Britt-Marie Was Here” can be enjoyed for its own merits. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9217547907387279288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1508122661" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jessica Jeffers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/188447-jessica-jeffers"><img alt="Jessica Jeffers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459125628p2/188447.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1508122661?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Jeffers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Jeffers" href="/user/show/188447-jessica-jeffers">Jessica Jeffers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28436716-britt-marie-was-here">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/188447-jessica-jeffers?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/188447-jessica-jeffers?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1508122661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6884824534684964984">I feel like the jerkiest of jerks here, but I was honestly just kind of bored with this one. If you liked Backman's <i>A Man Called Ove</i>, there's a good chance that you will like this one, too. It feels very familiar, with its tale of a stubborn senior citizen won over and softened by the bigger world. In my <i>Ove</i> review, I commented that Backman toed the line of treacly without falling completely in. Maybe he finally fell; I think that reading another book that was so similar thematically was just to</span>
  <span id="freeText6884824534684964984" style="display:none">I feel like the jerkiest of jerks here, but I was honestly just kind of bored with this one. If you liked Backman's <i>A Man Called Ove</i>, there's a good chance that you will like this one, too. It feels very familiar, with its tale of a stubborn senior citizen won over and softened by the bigger world. In my <i>Ove</i> review, I commented that Backman toed the line of treacly without falling completely in. Maybe he finally fell; I think that reading another book that was so similar thematically was just too much saccharine for me. <i>Britt-Marie</i> was fine, but I felt like I was reading something I'd already gone through before and I found myself struggling to engage. Because I'm a jerk. </span>

<div id="review_2414072639" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2414072639" />
    <a title="Phrynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne"><img alt="Phrynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577753809p2/8655084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2414072639?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8655084-phrynne?shelf=5000-books">5000-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2414072639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1764144146134342230">Another book by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6485178.Fredrik_Backman' title='Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fredrik Backman</a> which I find I cannot rate as highly as most people are doing. Perhaps he is just not the author for me. There was a lot to enjoy in this book, but there were also things which I felt did not work.<br/><br/>My biggest disappointment was with Britt-Marie herself. It was as though the author gave her characteristics, dialogue and a back story designed to provide pathos, humour and quirkiness but forgot to meld them into the one person. She was a conglomerate of separate parts</span>
  <span id="freeText1764144146134342230" style="display:none">Another book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6485178.Fredrik_Backman" title="Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">Fredrik Backman</a> which I find I cannot rate as highly as most people are doing. Perhaps he is just not the author for me. There was a lot to enjoy in this book, but there were also things which I felt did not work.<br /><br />My biggest disappointment was with Britt-Marie herself. It was as though the author gave her characteristics, dialogue and a back story designed to provide pathos, humour and quirkiness but forgot to meld them into the one person. She was a conglomerate of separate parts and I could not believe in the whole. How could someone so helpless that she disappeared entirely for decades in the shadow of her husband suddenly find the gumption to walk out the way she does? Why would everyone she meets instantly like her when she is so rude and socially inept?<br /><br />I struggled with the first part of the story but then got caught up in the characters and was really enjoying it. And then came the very long drawn out and totally uninformative ending. It was such an anticlimax and I still do not really know what happened. If any of my Goodreads friends are reading this who did understand please pm me and let me know.<br /><br />Overall three stars because I did enjoy the story, Britt-Marie was frequently funny,several of the other characters were really well drawn and the author does write nicely.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1764144146134342230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1657729884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1657729884" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3642045-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274829293p2/3642045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1657729884?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/3642045-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=sweden">sweden</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1657729884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17338720935826919864">My regard for soccer is increasing and my thoughts about "dying" or struggling towns is evolving. Thanks to the town of Borg and Britt-Marie. Dying relationships and dying economies come together in this novel of a late middle-aged woman who has left her old life with no real idea of who she is or where she's going -- physically, geographically or emotionally. Backman's book is her journey of self-discovery and her/Borg's discovery of each other.<br/><br/>Britt-Marie has been a wife and homemaker for her </span>
  <span id="freeText17338720935826919864" style="display:none">My regard for soccer is increasing and my thoughts about "dying" or struggling towns is evolving. Thanks to the town of Borg and Britt-Marie. Dying relationships and dying economies come together in this novel of a late middle-aged woman who has left her old life with no real idea of who she is or where she's going -- physically, geographically or emotionally. Backman's book is her journey of self-discovery and her/Borg's discovery of each other.<br /><br />Britt-Marie has been a wife and homemaker for her entire adult life but now circumstances have led her to a point where she must change---and this is so difficult for her. She is a woman of routines. How is she to leave behind a lifetime of tending to a home and husband, cleaning "just so" with exceptional care. Well she hopes the employment service will help her. The tiny town of Borg had no idea what was coming---and neither did Britt-Marie.<br /><br />At times I truly wondered about this woman--then I reached my first laugh out loud moment. From there on, I may have wondered slightly but I didn't question where Backman was going. I simply rode along. While I often am reading some heavy tomes, I do enjoy finding a book like this, where powerful messages are put forth in deceptively simple prose.<br /><br />A copy of this book was provided by the publisher through NetGalley in return for an honest review.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1634810115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7431655921508487985"><b>3.5 Stars</b><p>
  <b>"You are not alone if someone needs you."</b>
</p><p>Backman does it again....creates a one-of-a-kind quirky character, but this one just wants to be loved, needed and remembered.</p><p>The laughs begin early on as an honest <i>(to a fault)</i> and forthright 63 year old Britt-Marie enters into a conversation with a girl working in the unemployment office. Desperately in need of a job to improve her self-esteem and <b>need</b> to be useful, Britt-Marie unknowingly proceeds to insult the girl with a so-called compli</p></span>
  <span id="freeText7431655921508487985" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><p>
  <b>"You are not alone if someone needs you."</b>
</p><p>Backman does it again....creates a one-of-a-kind quirky character, but this one just wants to be loved, needed and remembered.</p><p>The laughs begin early on as an honest <i>(to a fault)</i> and forthright 63 year old Britt-Marie enters into a conversation with a girl working in the unemployment office. Desperately in need of a job to improve her self-esteem and <b>need</b> to be useful, Britt-Marie unknowingly proceeds to insult the girl with a so-called compliment about her hairstyle that will <b>crack you up!</b>. There the relationship and daily harassment begins and <b>does not end</b> until temporary employment is secured in the little ghost-like town of Borg.</p><p><b>BRITT-MARIE WAS HERE</b> started off really strong for me, but lost momentum when the storyline moved to Borg; picked up again when Matt <i>(the husband)</i> and Sven <i>(the policeman)</i> entered the picture, but lulled again with an ending a bit too ambiguous for me.</p><p>Overall, a very strong 3.5 Star read.</p></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1900369242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3065979907302181448">Being a bit sceptical to begin with, I ended up loving this book! <br/>The thing that had me sceptical was the protagonist, Britt-Marie, who is quite a character! She lives according to rules, traditions and norms, and she constantly worries about what other people think of her. This makes her quite a rude and quirky character that I wasn't sure I was up for reading a whole book about. However, I stuck with it and quickly found myself loving her and her quirkiness - how did that happen? <br/>The things th</span>
  <span id="freeText3065979907302181448" style="display:none">Being a bit sceptical to begin with, I ended up loving this book! <br />The thing that had me sceptical was the protagonist, Britt-Marie, who is quite a character! She lives according to rules, traditions and norms, and she constantly worries about what other people think of her. This makes her quite a rude and quirky character that I wasn't sure I was up for reading a whole book about. However, I stuck with it and quickly found myself loving her and her quirkiness - how did that happen? <br />The things that made me love this book are: Britt-Marie, the town of Borg and all of its (10?) inhabitants, the humour, the dynamic characters, and the open ending is what convinced me in the end that this is one of the best books I've read so far this year! <br />I'm going to miss Britt-Marie, Borg and all of its inhabitants, but I'm also going to cherish looking at the book on my shelves, remembering the great and touching story that it brought me. </span>

<div id="review_1660426267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1660426267" />
    <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma"><img alt="PattyMacDotComma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577835191p2/1128612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1660426267?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PattyMacDotComma" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma">PattyMacDotComma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=chcc-library">chcc-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=older-folks">older-folks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=fiction-adult">fiction-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1660426267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7794512990956262620">5★<br/>Loved it! Britt-Marie is an unappreciated social misfit, overlooked and living in the shadows of people who are more important, much like the author’s famous Ove from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18774964.A_Man_Called_Ove' title='A Man Called Ove by Fredrik Backman' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Man Called Ove</a>. She is as stubbornly awkward and set in her ways as Ove. <br/><br/>She wonders why people look offended or startled when she says things to be sociable.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“It’s very courageous of you to wear your hair so short when you have such a large forehead.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>or<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“It was very brave of you, putting that tie on. Because it looks abso</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText7794512990956262620" style="display:none">5★<br />Loved it! Britt-Marie is an unappreciated social misfit, overlooked and living in the shadows of people who are more important, much like the author’s famous Ove from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18774964.A_Man_Called_Ove" title="A Man Called Ove by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">A Man Called Ove</a>. She is as stubbornly awkward and set in her ways as Ove. <br /><br />She wonders why people look offended or startled when she says things to be sociable.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“It’s very courageous of you to wear your hair so short when you have such a large forehead.”</i>
</b><br /><br />or<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“It was very brave of you, putting that tie on. Because it looks absolutely preposterous.”</i>
</b><br /><br />She judges people by the state of their cutlery drawers, with cutlery arranged in the ‘right’ order. She is a fuss-pot who always carries baking soda to disinfect everything everywhere—chairs, rugs, window sills. <br /><br />She grew up in the shadow of her popular, beloved (now late) sister and eventually married Kent, one of the brothers whom they both knew and who has been married before. Kent is an entrepreneur who has many deals and meetings with “the Germans”. <br /><br />We meet her when Kent seems to be out of the picture (greener pastures, we suspect - she has mentioned his shirts always smelling of pizza she hasn’t shared and perfume she doesn’t wear).<br /><br />She goes to the employment bureau, expecting to be given a job forthwith. An employee tells her they’ll be in touch, so Britt-Marie returns the following day.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“The girls clears her throat. ‘Look, I’d love to talk further, but as I keep trying to tell you I just don’t have time at the moment.’’<br /><br />‘When do you have time?’ Britt-Marie asks, getting out her notebook and methodically going through a list. ‘Three o’clock?’<br /><br />‘I’m fully booked today—‘ <br /><br />‘I could also manage four or even five o’clock,’ Britt-Marie offers, conferring with herself.<br /><br />‘We close at five today,’ says the girl.<br /><br />‘Let’s say five o’clock then.’ <br /><br />‘What? No, we close at five—‘<br /><br />‘We certainly can’t have a meeting later than five, ‘ Britt-Marie protests.<br /><br />‘What?’ says the girl.<br /><br />Britt-Marie smiles with enormous, enormous patience.<br /><br />‘I don’t want to cause a scene here. Not at all. But my dear girl, civilised people have their dinner at six, so any later than five is surely a bit on the late side for a meeting, wouldn’t you agree? Or are you saying we should have our meeting while we’re eating?’<br /><br />‘No . . . I mean . . . What?’<br /><br />‘Ha. Well, in that case you have to make sure you’re not late. So the potatoes don’t get cold.’<br /><br />Then she writes ’18.00 Dinner’ on her list.<br /><br />The girl calls out something behind Britt-Marie but Britt-Marie has already gone, because she actually doesn’t have time to stand here going on about this all day."</i>
</b><br /><br />Britt-Marie returns at 5 to cook dinner at the office, and during the meal tells the girl about an article she’d read about a woman who was found dead in her flat after several weeks because of the smell.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“ ‘She had no children and no husband and no job. No one knew she was there. If one has a job, people notice if one doesn’t show up.<br /><br />. . . <br /><br />“I want a job because I actually don’t think it’s very edifying to disturb the neighbours with bad smells. I want someone to know I’m here.”</i>
</b><br /><br />She ends up in the tiny village of Borg which has a delightful assortment of entertaining characters, none of whom understand her (or vice-versa), but she treats them all the same—drunks, hoodlums, orphans, cops—and they certainly can’t ignore her. <br /><br />It's not all fun and games. Tragedy does strike closing-down places like Borg. The poverty and lack of opportunity is palpable, many children are neglected, and worst of all, for Britt-Marie, dirty. And noisy. <br /><br />But they love their football, and she starts washing their gear at the deserted Recreation Centre she is “managing” and learns about the game in spite of herself.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Every time one of the children gets the ball, their teammates are shouting: Here! I’m here!”</i>
</b><br /><br />An old former player sitting with Britt-Marie mutters <b>
  <i>“If you can be heard then you exist”.<br /><br />“The children play. Call out. Explain where they are. Britt-Marie squeezes her container of bicarbonate of soda until it has dents in it.<br /><br />‘I’m here,’ she whispers, wishing that Sven was here so she could tell him.<br /> <br />It’s a remarkable club. A remarkable game.”</i>
</b><br /><br />It’s a remarkable book with an unexpected ending.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7794512990956262620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1716559317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1716559317" />
    <a title="abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44478099-abby"><img alt="abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597252036p2/44478099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1716559317?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="abby" href="/user/show/44478099-abby">abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1716559317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5495540209584882767">You see, Britt-Marie does not judge people. No, certainly not. That would be uncivilized.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Britt-Marie would obviously never consider the woman to be "fat," because Britt-Marie is absolutely not the kind of person who pigeonholes people like that, but it does strike her how wonderful it must be for the woman to go through life so untroubled by her cholesterol levels."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Again, you see, it's just a matter of their being a wrong way to do things and a correct way. A clean, hygienic way. Unfortunat</span>
  <span id="freeText5495540209584882767" style="display:none">You see, Britt-Marie does not judge people. No, certainly not. That would be uncivilized.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Britt-Marie would obviously never consider the woman to be "fat," because Britt-Marie is absolutely not the kind of person who pigeonholes people like that, but it does strike her how wonderful it must be for the woman to go through life so untroubled by her cholesterol levels."</i>
</b><br /><br />Again, you see, it's just a matter of their being a wrong way to do things and a correct way. A clean, hygienic way. Unfortunately, and quite baffling to Britt-Marie, no one seems to care for, appreciate, or even <i>notice</i> the correct and clean and hygienic way of doing things. For years, Britt-Marie had dinner ready at six o'clock, as any person not raised by wolves would, and her husband Kent never said a word in thanks. He never commented on her carefully crafted hairstyle or paid attention to her superior use of baking soda. Never complimented her cooking without having to be asked first.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Britt-Marie doesn't know when their marriage slipped out of her hands. When it became worn and scratched up no matter how many coasters were used."</i>
</b><br /><br />Britt-Marie spent so much her life worrying about what other people thought of her, of how scandalous it would be to have someone see an unmade bed or muddy shoes tracking on the floor, only to realize at age 63 that no one's thought about her much at all. And Kent's been having an affair. For the first time in decades, she's on her own and looking for work.<br /><br />Borg is the type of town the world forgot. It sits along the side of a highway, gutted and turned into ghost town by the financial crisis (a reasoning Britt-Marie doesn't trust because, after all, Kent said the financial crisis was over, and Kent was an entrepreneur). Britt-Marie is sent there to work a temporary position at the recreation center. Soon she finds herself the coach of a rag tag team of soccer youths, despite having no interest in the sport whatsoever. For the first time in her life, Britt-Marie needs to figure out just who Britt-Marie is when she's not living for someone else.<br /><br />I'm a fan of Fredrik Backman's particular brand of emotional manipulation, and I very much enjoyed this book. It definitely has similarities to <i>A Man Called Ove</i> although it's not as well-done. I think Ove fans will be very much at home with Britt-Marie.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5495540209584882767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sHPMp7zaObFf/Ag3UCVIfwmKvmPP1vJSy7BH2sUq/X+30LKGfdcUteXNBfaUBtoukXXHgyQ31vaUI3PWcumTHg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Hqp173B6ASERZBHae1yUidTjwyEOkfCzbJXUgI/fQ3gZCQvOsXcsJatVHBu/fwbYTBy6weVw1BczBuCMOBwtGQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6485178.Fredrik_Backman">About Fredrik Backman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/6485178.Fredrik_Backman"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1493098924p3/6485178.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>

31,112
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12547434890740229248">Fredrik Backman is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of A Man Called Ove (soon to be a major motion picture starring Tom Hanks), My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She’s Sorry, Britt-Marie Was Here, Beartown, Us Against You, as well as two novellas, And Every Morning the Way Home Gets Longer and Longer and The Deal of a Lifetime. Things My Son Needs to Know About the World, his first work </span>
  <span id="freeText12547434890740229248" style="display:none">Fredrik Backman is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of A Man Called Ove (soon to be a major motion picture starring Tom Hanks), My Grandmother Asked Me to Tell You She’s Sorry, Britt-Marie Was Here, Beartown, Us Against You, as well as two novellas, And Every Morning the Way Home Gets Longer and Longer and The Deal of a Lifetime. Things My Son Needs to Know About the World, his first work of non-fiction, will be released in the US in May 2019. His books are published in more than forty countries. He lives in Stockholm, Sweden, with his wife and two children. Connect with him on Twitter @BackmanLand or on Instagram @backmansk.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12547434890740229248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
